Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
5 min
Who Was Imam Sanusi? His Titles and Lineage
Biographical introduction listing Sanusi's titles and explaining his nisbas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly credentials and noble lineage of Imam Sanusi as recorded in his biographical introduction.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi's name tells us his tribe, his school, and his noble descent.

This passage is not a theological argument but a biographical sketch. It introduces Imam Sanusi with a cascade of honorific titles and then explains the meaning behind each nisba. It shows how classical scholars were identified by their expertise, school, and ancestry.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the dense list of honorifics at the beginning.
2
Identify the titles given to Sanusi
List the titles: master of theologians, all-knowing imam, versatile, hadith scholar, reciter, jurist, fundamentalist, verifier, Sufi, pious, abstinent. Consider what each title says about his expertise.
These titles establish his authority in multiple sciences.
3
Understand the different nisbas
The passage explains nisbas: al-Sanusi (tribal), al-Tilimsani (place), al-Maliki (school), al-Ash'ari (theology), al-Tawhidi (specialty). Also al-Isawi, al-Sharif, al-Qurashi, al-Qassar from his handwriting. Trace each nisba's origin.
Nisbas often indicate tribal lineage, geographical origin, or scholarly affiliation.
4
Appreciate the value of biographical introductions
Ask yourself why classical texts begin with such biographies. They authenticate the author's credibility and situate him within the scholarly tradition.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام السنوسي
شيخ متكلّمي عصره ومصره ، الإمام العلامة المشارك ، المحدث المُقرِئ ، الفقيه الأصولي المحقق ، الصوفي التقي الورع ؛ أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي التلمساني المالكي الأشعري التوحيدي
والسنوسي : نسبة إلى سَنُوسة ؛ قبيلة من البرابرة في المغرب ، قال العلامة الزبيدي في «تاج العروس » : ( وإليهم نسب الولي الصالح أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي ؛ لأنه نزل عندهم ، وقيل : بل هو منهم ، وأمه شريفة حسنية ، كذا حققه سيدي محمد بن إبراهيم الملالي في « المواهب القدسية » ووجد بخطّهِ على ( شرح الآجرومية ( له : « السنوسي العيسي الشريف القرشي القصَّار » ، قلت : العيسي : من بيت عيسى والتوحيدي : نسبة للاشتغال بعلم التوحيد ، كذا ذكر الحفناوي
Biography of Imam al-Sanusi: The master of the theologians of his time and his region, the imam, the all-knowing scholar, the versatile, the hadith scholar, the reciter, the jurist, the fundamentalist, the verifier, the Sufi, the pious, the abstinent; Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi al-Tilimsani al-Maliki al-Ash'ari al-Tawhidi. And 'al-Sanusi' is a relative attribution to Sanusa, a tribe of the Berbers in the Maghreb. Allamah al-Zabidi said in 'Taj al-Arus': 'To them is attributed the righteous saint Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi, because he settled among them, and it is said he is from them, and his mother was a Sharifah Hasaniyyah.' Thus verified by my master Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Malali in 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyyah'. And found in his own handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajurrumiyyah: 'Al-Sanusi al-Isawi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar.' I say: 'al-Isawi' is from the house of Isa, and 'al-Tawhidi' is a relative attribution to occupation with the science of tawhid, as mentioned by al-Hifnawi.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam Sanusi. It first lists his honorific titles: master of the theologians of his time and region, all-knowing imam, versatile scholar, hadith scholar, reciter, jurist, fundamentalist verifier, Sufi, pious, and abstinent. Then it gives his full name: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shu'ayb al-Sanusi, with the place and school attributions: al-Tilimsani (from Tlemcen), al-Maliki (Maliki school), al-Ash'ari (Ash'ari theology), and al-Tawhidi (specialist in tawhid). The passage then explains the nisba 'al-Sanusi' by tracing it to a Berber tribe called Sanusa, citing al-Zabidi's Taj al-Arus. It notes that Sanusi settled among them and some say he is from them, and his mother was a Sharifah Hasaniyyah (descendant of the Prophet through Hasan). This verification is attributed to Muhammad al-Malali in 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyyah'. The passage further mentions that in Sanusi's own handwriting on his commentary on the Ajurrumiyyah, he wrote the nisbas 'al-Isawi' (from the house of Isa, i.e., Hasanid lineage), 'al-Sharif' (noble), 'al-Qurashi' (Quraysh), and 'al-Qassar' (a trade: fuller). The author (of this biography) adds that 'al-Isawi' refers to the house of Isa, and 'al-Tawhidi' is derived from occupation with the science of tawhid, as mentioned by al-Hifnawi. The passage thus establishes Sanusi's scholarly credentials and noble lineage.

Key Terms
السنوسي
التوحيدي
الأشعري
سَنُوسة
البرابرة
تاج العروس
المواهب القدسية
شرح الآجرومية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi is a personal surname.
Correction: Sanusi is a nisba referring to the Berber tribe Sanusa.

Checkpoint
According to the biography, what is the origin of the nisba 'al-Sanusi'?
A) It is derived from the name of his father.
B) It refers to a town in Tunisia.
C) It is a relative attribution to a Berber tribe called Sanusa.
D) It is a title given by his teachers.

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi was a master theologian with a noble lineage, known by his tribal and scholarly attributions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have seen how Imam Sanusi earned titles like 'master of theologians' and 'al-Tawhidi' through dedicated study. What single title would you most like to be remembered for in your relationship with Allah, and what will you change in your daily routine to pursue it?
?
Sanusi was both a scholar of outward sciences (fiqh, hadith) and inward purification (Sufism). Which of these two dimensions do you neglect, and what is the first step you can take this week to restore balance?
?
His lineage combined Berber and Sharifian heritage. How does knowing that Allah judges by taqwa, not lineage, free you from pride or despair about your own ancestry? Will you consciously remind yourself of this the next time you feel superior or inferior because of your background?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner
5 min
Imam al-Sanusi's Titles and Lineage
Biographical introduction naming Imam al-Sanusi's titles and explaining his nisbas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various titles and nisbas of Imam al-Sanusi and their significance in identifying his scholarly and spiritual identity.

Core Idea
The names of a scholar tell the story of his knowledge, lineage, and affiliation.

This lesson introduces the biographical context of Imam al-Sanusi, the author of the matn we are studying. Understanding his full name and titles helps us appreciate his authority in kalam. The passage lists his many attributes and explains each nisba.

Guided Path
1
Identify his eminent titles
Read the opening list of titles such as 'master of theologians', 'imam', 'hadith scholar', etc. Note how these establish his scholarly stature.
These titles cover multiple disciplines: theology, jurisprudence, hadith, Sufism.
2
Learn his full name
Read his full name: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shuayb al-Sanusi... This gives his lineage and key affiliations.
Each part of the name carries meaning.
3
Understand the nisba 'al-Sanusi'
The passage explains 'al-Sanusi' refers to the Sanusa tribe of Berbers in the Maghrib. Note the commentary on his mother being a sharifa.
This connects him to the Prophet's family.
4
Explore other nisbas
Read about al-Mallali, al-Isawi, al-Sharif, al-Qurashi, and al-Tawhidi. Pay attention to the meaning of 'al-Tawhidi' as related to the science of tawhid.
The nisba 'al-Tawhidi' is especially relevant to our study.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام السنوسي
شيخ متكلّمي عصره ومصره ، الإمام العلامة المشارك ، المحدث المُقرِئ ، الفقيه الأصولي المحقق ، الصوفي التقي الورع ؛ أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي التلمساني المالكي الأشعري التوحيدي
والسنوسي : نسبة إلى سَنُوسة ؛ قبيلة من البرابرة في المغرب ، قال العلامة الزبيدي في «تاج العروس » : ( وإليهم نسب الولي الصالح أبو عبد الله محمد بن يوسف بن عمر بن شعيب السنوسي ؛ لأنه نزل عندهم ، وقيل : بل هو منهم ، وأمه شريفة حسنية (١) ، كذا حققه سيدي محمد بن إبراهيم الملالي في « المواهب القدسية »(۲) ووجد بخطّهِ على ( شرح الآجرومية ( له : « السنوسي العيسي الشريف القرشي القصَّار » ، قلت : العيسي : من بيت عيسى والتوحيدي : نسبة للاشتغال بعلم التوحيد ، كذا ذكر الحفناوي
(١) لعله أراد جدته أم أبيه كما سترى
(۲) المَلالي : نسبة إلى مَلالة بوزان جَبَّانة؛ قرية قرب بجاية، و«المواهب القدسية» : كذا في المخطوط الذي بين أيدينا، وطبع باسم : المواهب القدوسية»، والله أعلم.
(۳) تاج العروس ( س ن س ) ، وانظر ( البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان » ( ص ۲۳۷ )
Translation of Imam al-Sanusi: The master of the theologians of his time and his country, the imam, the all-knowing, the collaborator, the hadith scholar, the reciter, the jurist, the foundational scholar, the researcher, the Sufi, the pious, the devout; Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shuayb al-Sanusi al-Tilimsani al-Maliki al-Ash'ari al-Tawhidi. Al-Sanusi: a relative attribution to Sanusa, a tribe of the Berbers in the Maghrib. Al-Allama al-Zubaydi said in Taj al-Arus: "Attributed to them is the righteous saint Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shuayb al-Sanusi, because he settled among them, and it is said he is from them. His mother is a sharifa from the line of Hasan (1), as verified by my master Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Mallali in al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya (2). And found in his own handwriting on his commentary on al-Ajurrumiyya: 'al-Sanusi al-Isawi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar.' I say: al-Isawi: from the house of Isa, and al-Tawhidi: relative to occupation with the science of tawhid, as mentioned by al-Hafnawi. (1) Perhaps he meant his grandmother, his father's mother, as you will see. (2) Al-Mallali: relative to Mallala, with the measure of Jabbana, a village near Bijaya. Al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya: thus in the manuscript in our hands, and printed under the name al-Mawahib al-Qudusiyya, and God knows best. (3) Taj al-Arus (s.n.s.), and see al-Bustan fi Dhikr al-Awliya wal-Ulama bi-Tilimsan p. 237.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction. It begins by listing Imam al-Sanusi's lofty titles: 'master of the theologians of his time and country', 'all-knowing imam', 'collaborator', 'hadith scholar', 'reciter', 'jurist', 'foundational researcher', 'Sufi, pious, devout'. Then it gives his full name: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Umar ibn Shuayb al-Sanusi al-Tilimsani al-Maliki al-Ash'ari al-Tawhidi. The author then explains each nisba. First, 'al-Sanusi' is traced to the Sanusa tribe of Berbers in the Maghrib, citing al-Zubaydi's Taj al-Arus for details about his lineage and the claim that his mother was a sharifa from the line of Hasan, with a footnote clarifying 'mother' as 'grandmother'. Second, 'al-Mallali' is explained as relative to Mallala, a village near Bijaya. The author mentions finding in al-Sanusi's own handwriting an additional nisba: 'al-Isawi al-Sharif al-Qurashi al-Qassar'. He comments that 'al-Isawi' means from the house of Isa, and 'al-Tawhidi' means occupied with the science of tawhid, as stated by al-Hafnawi. The passage ends with a footnote reference to Taj al-Arus and another work. The author's purpose is to establish the full identity and noble lineage of Imam al-Sanusi.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The nisba 'al-Tawhidi' refers to a sect or group.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that 'al-Tawhidi' is a relative attribution to occupation with the science of tawhid (Islamic monotheism), not to a sect.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the origin of the nisba 'al-Sanusi'?
A) A city in Algeria
B) A tribe of Berbers in Morocco
C) A village near Bijaya
D) A family of scholars

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's name reflects his deep learning, his Maliki and Ash'ari affiliation, and his noble lineage traced to the Prophet through Hasan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Sanusi carried multiple nisbas linking him to a tribe, a city, a madhab, an aqeeda, and a science. Which of these affiliations do you think is most important for a believer to have today? And more importantly, which one is most lacking in your own life? What is one concrete step you can take this week to strengthen that connection?
?
The passage notes ambiguity about whether 'his mother' actually means his grandmother. How do you react when you encounter uncertainty in religious texts or scholarly opinions? Do you dismiss it, or do you humbly say 'Allah knows best' as the author does? Reflect on an area where you have been too quick to assume certainty.

The Dispute Over Imam al-Sanusi's Birth Year
Discussion of conflicting reports on Imam al-Sanusi's birth year.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conflicting historical reports regarding Imam al-Sanusi's birth year and the reasons for the uncertainty.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi's birth year is uncertain due to conflicting reports from his own student.

This passage addresses a common challenge in biographical studies: establishing precise dates. For a figure as significant as Imam al-Sanusi, even his birth year is disputed. The text presents multiple accounts from his student al-Mallali and other scholars, showing why certainty is elusive and why reliable transmission matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice that the passage begins by stating the disagreement and then cites specific reports.
The passage includes footnotes; focus on the main text first.
2
Identify the conflicting reports
The passage gives at least three different ages at death mentioned by various sources. List them: 63 years (implied birth 832 AH), 55 years (implied birth 840 AH), and 56 years (implied birth around 834 AH?).
The third report from al-Balawi says 56 years at death.
3
Consider the reasons for uncertainty
Why is there disagreement? The passage suggests lack of clarity ('يرجع لعدم ذلك') and inconsistency in al-Mallali's transmission. Ask yourself what this tells us about historical record-keeping.
Even the closest student gave different accounts.
4
Reflect on the scholarly attitude
Note that some scholars like Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti simply said 'after 830 AH', showing caution. The passage does not resolve the dispute; it presents the evidence.
This teaches us to accept uncertainty when evidence conflicts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مولده ونشأته
يرجع لعدم ذلك اختلف في سنة ولادة الإمام السنوسي؛ وسبب نصه هو على ذلك، واضطراب نقل تلميذه الملالي في ذلك أيضاً، قال العلامة التُنْبُكْتي في ( نيل الابتهاج ) (۲) : ( رأيت مقيداً عن بعض العلماء : أنه سأل الملالي المذكور عن سنّ الشيخ ، فقال له : مات عن ثلاث وستين سنة ((٣) فعلى هذه الرواية : تكون السنة التي وُلد فيها الإمام السنوسي ( ٨٣٢هـ ) (٤) هي
(۱) تعريف الخلف برجال السلف ( ١ / ١٧٦ ) ، ومن الألقاب التي صاغها المؤرخ ابن القاضي المكناسي في ( درة الحجال » ( ١٤١/٢ ) أن قال : ( أبو عبد الله ، الإمام المعقولي الفقيه المحدث الفرضي الحيسوبي ) نسبة لعلوم المعقول وعلم الحساب
(۲) وقد لخص في هذا الكتاب سيرة الإمام السنوسي ، من كتاب « المواهب القدسية» لتلميذ الإمام السنوسي ؛ وهو الشيخ محمد بن عمر الملالي رحمه الله تعالى . . أحسن تلخيص
(۳) نيل الابتهاج ( ص ٥٧٠ ) .
(٤) وفي ( نيل الابتهاج » ( ص ٥٧٠ ) أيضاً نقل قول الملالي : ( وأخبرني قبل موته بنحو عام أنَّ سنّهُ خمس وخمسون سنة ) ، فتكون سنة ولادته على هذا ( ٨٤٠هـ ) ، والله أعلم ، ولهذا اكتفى ابن مريم والتنبكتي بقولهما : ( مولده بعد الثلاثين وثمان مئة ) ، وانظر ( البستان » ( ص ٢٤٤ ) ، وعندما ذكر العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي خبر وفاته في « ثبته » ( ص ٤٣٨ ) قال : ( وكانت سنه يومئذ ستاً وخمسين سنة )
His birth and upbringing. Due to the lack of that, there is disagreement about the year of Imam al-Sanusi's birth; and the reason for his own statement [on his age] is [unclear], and also the inconsistency in the transmission of his student al-Mallali concerning that. Al-Allama al-Tunbukti said in Nayl al-Ibtihaj (2): 'I saw a note from some scholars that he asked the aforementioned al-Mallali about the age of the Shaykh, and he said to him: He died at sixty-three years (3).' So according to this report, the year in which Imam al-Sanusi was born is (832 AH) (4). (1) Ta'rif al-Khalaf bi-Rijal al-Salaf (1/176), and among the epithets coined by the historian Ibn al-Qadi al-Miknasi in Durrat al-Hijal (2/141) he said: 'Abu Abdullah, the rationalist imam, the jurist, the hadith scholar, the faradi, the hisabi' relative to the rational sciences and the science of calculation. (2) And he summarized in this book the biography of Imam al-Sanusi from the book al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya of the student of Imam al-Sanusi, who is Shaykh Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali, may God have mercy on him... an excellent summary. (3) Nayl al-Ibtihaj (p. 570). (4) And in Nayl al-Ibtihaj (p. 570) also the saying of al-Mallali is transmitted: 'He informed me about a year before his death that his age was fifty-five years,' so his birth year according to this is (840 AH), and God knows best. For this reason, Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti sufficed with their statement: 'His birth was after 830 AH.' See al-Bustan (p. 244), and when al-Allama Abu Ja'far al-Balawi mentioned news of his death in his Thabt (p. 438), he said: 'His age at that time was fifty-six years.'
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage discusses the controversy surrounding Imam al-Sanusi's birth year. It begins by stating that due to lack of clarity and inconsistency in the transmission of his student al-Mallali, there is disagreement. The author then cites al-Tunbukti's report from Nayl al-Ibtihaj: al-Mallali was asked about the Shaykh's age and replied that he died at 63 years. Based on this, his birth would be 832 AH. The footnotes provide additional details: (1) lists other epithets coined by Ibn al-Qadi al-Miknasi. (2) explains that al-Tunbukti summarized al-Sanusi's biography from al-Mallali's book. (3) gives the page reference. (4) presents an alternative report from al-Mallali that the Imam said his age was 55 years a year before his death, giving a birth year of 840 AH. The footnote also notes that Ibn Maryam and al-Tunbukti simply say 'after 830 AH', and cites al-Balawi reporting the age at death as 56. The passage thus presents multiple conflicting accounts without definitively resolving them, showing the difficulty in establishing a precise birth year.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what birth year for Imam al-Sanusi does the report from al-Mallali that he died at 63 years imply?
A) 832 AH
B) 840 AH
C) 830 AH
D) 836 AH

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's exact birth year remains uncertain due to conflicting accounts from his student al-Mallali and other sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When faced with conflicting reports about a religious figure's life, do you tend to pick the one that fits your narrative or accept the uncertainty? How does this lesson challenge you to be honest about what we do not know?
?
Imagine you were al-Mallali, transmitting details about your teacher's age. Your two reports differ by eight years. What would it take for you to admit the inconsistency? Are you willing to be transparent about your own uncertainties in matters of faith?
?
If the birth year of a great scholar like Imam al-Sanusi is unclear despite multiple witnesses, how much more careful must you be before claiming certainty about lesser-known matters? Will you commit to saying 'Allahu a'lam' more often?

Life of Imam al-Sanusi

Sanusi's Uphringing and His Father's Virtue
Description of Sanusi's family background and father's piety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the pious environment that shaped Imam al-Sanusi's early education and the virtuous character of his father.

Core Idea
Sanusi's father was a humble Quran teacher and a saint; his upbringing was blessed.

This passage provides a glimpse into the family background of the great scholar. It recounts how he was raised in a household of virtue and knowledge, learning from his pious father. The description of his father's character and profession sets the stage for appreciating Sanusi's own spiritual and scholarly achievements.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get a sense of the overall context and flow.
2
Identify key persons
Notice the mention of Imam al-Sanusi, his father Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, and the scholar al-Mallali who quotes the father's description.
3
Analyze the father's description
Read carefully the qualities attributed to the father by al-Mallali: piety, asceticism, humility, good manners, etc.
4
Note the father's profession
The text explicitly states the father's craft was teaching the Quran to children. This shows the humble origins of the Imam's education.
This corrects a potential misconception about the father being a highly advanced scholar.
5
Reflect on the spiritual environment
Consider how the father's piety and the mention of miracles (كرامات) and spiritual insight relate to Sanusi's own development.

نشأ الإمام السنوسي في بيت فضل وعلم؛ فوالده هو الشيخ (1) الصالح الزاهد الخاشع الأستاذ المحقق يوسف أبو يعقوب، وعنه أخذ الإمام مبادئ العلوم، وكان ذلك في تلمسان حاضرة العلم يومها، وطينة الأولياء والصالحين. وجدة الإمام السنوسي لأبيه كانت حسنيَّةَ النسب، ولذا قد يلقب الإمام السنوسي بالحسني من جهة والدة أبيه (٢)، وقال الشيخ الملالي في صفة والد الإمام: (كان سيدي يوسف السنوسي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه وعن شيخنا ابنه.. رجلاً صالحاً ورعاً، خاشعاً الله تعالى زاهداً [في] الدنيا معرضاً عنها، مقبلاً على طاعة الله تعالى، سالم الصدر، حسن الأخلاق، ومبتسماً في وجه كل من لقاه، حسن المعاشرة، كريم الطبع)(٣) وكانت حرفة هذا الوالد المبارك هي إقراء القرآن للأولاد في المكتب، ويظهر من كلام الشيخ الملالي أنّ عناية الله قد رافقته من طفولته، فأجرى الله على يديه الكرامات وكشف عن بصيرته.
Imam al-Sanusi grew up in a house of virtue and knowledge; his father is the pious, ascetic, humble, verified teacher Yusuf Abu Ya'qub (1), and from him the Imam took the principles of the sciences, and that was in Tlemcen, the capital of knowledge at that time, and the nature of the saints and righteous. And the grandmother of Imam al-Sanusi on his father's side was of Hasanid lineage, so the Imam may be called al-Hasani from the side of his father's mother (2). And al-Mallali said in describing the Imam's father: (My master Yusuf al-Sanusi, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him and with our sheikh his son... was a righteous, pious man, humble before Allah, ascetic in the world, turning away from it, devoted to the obedience of Allah, clear-hearted, good-mannered, smiling in the face of everyone he met, good in companionship, noble in nature) (3). And the craft of this blessed father was teaching the Quran to children in the school, and it appears from al-Mallali's words that the care of Allah accompanied him from his childhood, so Allah worked miracles at his hands and unveiled his insight.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage describes the early environment and family background of Imam al-Sanusi. It first notes that he grew up in a house of virtue and knowledge. His father, Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, is described as a pious, ascetic, and verified teacher, from whom the Imam learned the foundations of the sciences in Tlemcen, a city known for knowledge and saints. The text also mentions that the Imam's paternal grandmother was of Hasanid lineage, so he is sometimes called al-Hasani. Then a quotation from al-Mallali portrays the father's character in detail: he was righteous, humble, ascetic, cheerful, and noble. Finally, the passage reveals that the father's profession was teaching the Quran to children, and that from his childhood, Allah's care accompanied the Imam, manifesting in miracles and spiritual insight. This establishes the blessed environment that shaped the Imam.

Key Terms

يوسف أبو يعقوب
الملالي
الحسني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi's father was a renowned scholar of advanced Islamic sciences.
Correction: The text explicitly states his profession was teaching the Quran to children (إقراء القرآن للأولاد في المكتب). He was a pious saint, but not a high-level academic scholar.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Sanusi's early environment was one of piety, asceticism, and Quranic teaching, with his saintly father as his first teacher.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you honor your parents as much as Imam al-Sanusi honored his father, who was merely a Quran teacher? What would it take for you to see the barakah in your own father's humble work?
?
Your father may not be a scholar, but does his character reflect the attributes of Sanusi's father—humility, cheerfulness, and piety? If not, how can you lovingly encourage him toward that path, starting with your own example?
?
When you meet people, do you smile at them like Yusuf al-Sanusi did? What holds you back from being 'good in companionship' and 'noble in nature' with those you encounter daily?

Sanusi's Teachers and Spiritual Blessings
Brief note on Sanusi's teachers and spiritual care.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the traditional sources of Imam al-Sanusi's knowledge: formal study with elite scholars and spiritual blessings from saints.

Core Idea
Sanusi's knowledge came from both books and blessings.

This brief passage from the biographical tradition highlights how Imam al-Sanusi acquired knowledge through two complementary channels: the formal study with renowned scholars of his time, and the spiritual attention of saints. It reminds us that in the Islamic scholarly tradition, knowledge is not merely academic but also blessed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the two sources mentioned.
The passage uses the term 'lahazat' which has a deeper meaning.
2
Identify the two sources of knowledge
Find the phrases that refer to formal study and spiritual blessing. Note the contrast between 'ulama' and 'awliya'.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why the author includes both scholars and saints. What does this say about the nature of knowledge in Islam?
This passage shows the importance of spiritual transmission alongside academic learning.

أخذ الإمام السنوسي العلم عن جلة علماء عصره ولحظات الأولياء والصالحين. ونالته عناية

Commentary
This short passage states that Imam al-Sanusi acquired knowledge from the major scholars of his era ('jilla 'ulama' 'asrihi') and from the 'glances' (lahazat) of the saints and righteous, meaning their spiritual attention and care. It also says he received divine care. The footnotes refer to the work 'al-Mawahib al-Qudsiyya' as the source for this information, noting that it is the first work to describe him with these titles. While brief, the passage highlights the two sources of his knowledge: formal study with scholars and informal spiritual blessing from saints.

What change in your intention will you make before your next lesson?

Imam Sanusi's Early Life and Father
Describes Imam Sanusi's father, lineage, and early upbringing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early upbringing of Imam al-Sanusi, including the character of his father and the environment that shaped him.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi's virtuous upbringing shaped his scholarly legacy.

Imam al-Sanusi is one of the most important figures in Ash'ari theology. Before we study his works, it is essential to know the environment that produced him. This passage from his biography describes his father's piety, his lineage, and the scholarly atmosphere of Tlemcen.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview. Notice the flow from upbringing to father's description to al-Mallali's quote.
The passage is rich in descriptive language about character.
2
Examine the father's attributes
Identify the qualities given to his father: pious, ascetic, humble, teacher, verifier. Reflect on how these traits would influence a child's education.
Note that the father was a Quran teacher to children.
3
Consider the setting: Tlemcen
Tlemcen is described as a center of knowledge and saints. Think about how the environment contributes to scholarly growth.
The phrase 'clay of saints and righteous' is metaphorical.
4
Reflect on the lineage
The passage mentions Hasanid lineage through his grandmother. Why might this be significant in a biographical introduction?
This explains the occasional title 'al-Hasani'.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Connect all parts: how does this background prepare us to understand Imam al-Sanusi's later contributions?
Consider the role of early upbringing in producing a scholar.

نشأ الإمام السنوسي في بيت فضل وعلم؛ فوالده هو الشيخ الصالح الزاهد الخاشع الأستاذ المحقق يوسف أبو يعقوب، وعنه أخذ الإمام مبادئ العلوم، وكان ذلك في تلمسان حاضرة العلم يومها، وطينة الأولياء والصالحين. وجدة الإمام السنوسي لأبيه كانت حسنيَّةَ النسب، ولذا قد يلقب الإمام السنوسي بالحسني من جهة والدة أبيه. وقال الشيخ الملالي في صفة والد الإمام: ( كان سيدي يوسف السنوسي رحمه الله تعالى ورضي عنه وعن شيخنا ابنه .. رجلاً صالحاً ورعاً، خاشعاً الله تعالى زاهداً [في] الدنيا معرضاً عنها، مقبلاً على طاعة الله تعالى، سالم الصدر، حسن الأخلاق، ومبتسماً في وجه كل من لقاه، حسن المعاشرة، كريم الطبع ). وكانت حرفة هذا الوالد المبارك هي إقراء القرآن للأولاد في المكتب، ويظهر من كلام الشيخ الملالي أنّ عناية الله قد رافقته من طفولته، فأجرى الله على يديه الكرامات وكشف عن بصيرته.
Imam al-Sanusi grew up in a house of virtue and knowledge; his father was the pious, ascetic, humble teacher, the verifier, Yusuf Abu Ya'qub. From him the Imam took the principles of the sciences, and that was in Tlemcen, the center of knowledge in its day, and the clay of saints and righteous. The grandmother of Imam al-Sanusi on his father's side was of Hasanid lineage, so the Imam may be called al-Hasani from the side of his father's mother. And al-Mallali said describing the Imam's father: 'My master Yusuf al-Sanusi, may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him and with our master his son... was a righteous, devout man, humble before Allah, ascetic in this world, turning away from it, devoted to obeying Allah, pure-hearted, good-mannered, smiling in the face of everyone he met, good in companionship, noble in nature.' And the craft of this blessed father was teaching the Quran to children in the school (maktab). And it appears from al-Mallali's words that Allah's care accompanied him from his childhood, so Allah performed miracles at his hands and unveiled his insight.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam al-Sanusi's early life, focusing on his father and lineage. It begins by stating that al-Sanusi grew up in a household of virtue and knowledge. His father was Yusuf Abu Ya'qub, described as pious, ascetic, a scholar and verifier. The Imam learned the basics of the sciences from him in Tlemcen, a major center of learning and saints. The passage then mentions that his paternal grandmother was of Hasanid lineage (descendants of Hasan, grandson of the Prophet), which is why al-Sanusi is sometimes called al-Hasani. Then a quote from al-Mallali describes his father's character in detail: he was righteous, devout, humble, ascetic, pure-hearted, good-mannered, smiling, etc. His father's profession was teaching the Quran to children in a school. The passage concludes by noting that Allah's care accompanied him from childhood, and that miracles were performed at his hands and his insight was unveiled.

Imam al-Sanusi's Chain in Quranic Readings
al-Balawi's account of al-Sanusi's qira'at transmission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Sanusi's mastery of the seven Quranic readings (qira'at) is validated through a documented chain of teachers and ijazas, as recorded by al-Balawi.

Core Idea
His ijaza chain proves rigorous oral transmission of the seven readings.

This passage offers a window into the world of classical Quranic scholarship, where knowledge was transmitted through direct oral recitation and formal licensing (ijaza). Through an elaborate quote from al-Balawi, we see Imam al-Sanusi's credentials in qira'at and the distinguished teachers who authorized him, spanning multiple generations of master reciters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the formal names and titles—they indicate the high level of the teachers.
The passage begins with a strong claim of al-Sanusi's high standing, then supports it with al-Balawi's testimony.
2
Identify the main claim
The opening line states that al-Sanusi had 'high standing in the collection of Quranic readings'. This is the thesis of the passage.
The rest of the passage provides evidence for this claim.
3
Trace the chain of transmission
The quote from al-Balawi gives a step-by-step chain: al-Sanusi studied under Abu al-Hajjaj, who studied under two masters (al-Yaznasi and al-Laja'i), who in turn studied under two earlier scholars. Follow these links and notice the specific details (e.g., recitation amounts, ijaza).
This chain demonstrates the rigorous oral tradition.
4
Reflect on the significance of ijaza
Al-Balawi mentions that al-Sanusi received a 'general absolute license' (ijaza mutlaqa 'amma). Understand that ijaza is not just a certificate but a personal authorization based on direct audition and verification.
This practice ensures the authenticity of the transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكان للإمام السنوسي علوٌّ كعب في جمع القراءات؛ فقد قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي: ( أخذ القراءات السبع عن الفقيه الأستاذ العالم العامل المحقق المقرئ أبي الحجاج يوسف بن الشيخ الصالح أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني تلاوةً عليه في ختمتين، قال: وزدت من الثالثة قدراً صالحاً لم أتحقق الآن منتهاه جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن « التيسير » و « الشاطبية » وأجازه في المقارئ السبعة وفي غيرها من مروياته إجازة مطلقة عامة، وحدثه بالسبع عن الإمامين العالمين المدرسين: الأستاذ الجليل الأعرف الأشهر المقرئ المحقق الأدرك الخاشع أبي العباس أحمد بن أبي عمران موسى اليزناسني، والأستاذ الجليل المعظم الشهير المحقق الضابط المتقن النحوي اللغوي الحافظ الصالح الأزكى أبي العباس أحمد بن الفقيه العالم المتفنن أبي عبد الله محمد بن عيسى اللَّجائي، قراءةً على الأول جمعاً في ختمة للسبعة، قال: وزدت ثلاثة أحزاب من سورة البقرة، وعلى الثاني لـ « فاتحة الكتاب » و « البقرة » وأوائل « آل عمران » جمعاً للسبع، وإجازة فيما قرأ وفيما بقي، حدثاه معاً بذلك عن الأستاذين: أبي عبد الله القيسي وأبي الحجاج بن مبخوت بسندهما ). ومن جملة العلماء الذين قرأ عليهم: الشيخ العلامة نصر الزواوي، والشيخ العالم محمد بن تومرت الصنهاجي، والشيخ
And Imam al-Sanusi had high standing in the collection of Quranic readings (qira'at). The scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: 'He took the seven readings (al-qira'at al-sab') from the jurist, the teacher, the scholar, the practitioner, the verifier, the reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete recitations (khatmatayn). He said: And I added from a third a good amount whose extent I have not verified now, a collection of the seven according to what is contained in al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyyah. And he gave him a general absolute license in the seven readings and in other narrations, and he narrated the seven to him from the two imams, the two scholars, the two teachers: the venerable teacher, the most knowledgeable, the most famous, the reciter, the verifier, the insightful, the humble Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Abi Imran Musa al-Yaznasi and the venerable teacher, the magnified, the famous, the verifier, the exacting, the precise, the grammarian, the linguist, the memorizer, the righteous, the pure Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn al-Faqih al-Alim al-Mutafannin Abi Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Isa al-Laja'i. He recited to the first a collection in one complete recitation for the seven, and he said: I added three hizbs from Surat al-Baqarah, and to the second for Surat al-Fatihah, al-Baqarah, and the beginnings of Aal Imran as a collection for the seven, and a license for what he recited and for what remained. Both together narrated that from the two teachers: Abu Abd Allah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Makhkhut with their chains.' And among the scholars he studied with: the scholar al-Allamah Nasr al-Zawawi, and the scholar Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji, and the Shaykh...
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam al-Sanusi's expertise in Quranic readings (qira'at) and his chain of teachers. It begins by stating that al-Sanusi had high standing in the collection of qira'at. Then it quotes Abu Ja'far al-Balawi, who gives details of al-Sanusi's study of the seven readings. He studied under Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf al-Hasani, reciting to him two complete recitations and a third partial. He was authorized (ijaza) in the seven readings. Then the chain is traced back to two major teachers: Abu al-Abbas Ahmad al-Yaznasi and Abu al-Abbas Ahmad al-Laja'i. For the first, he recited a complete recitation, adding three hizbs; for the second, he recited specific suras. Both teachers narrated from Abu Abd Allah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Makhkhut with their chains. The passage then begins a list of other scholars he studied with, although the text cuts off at the end of the page. This demonstrates the rigorous transmission of qira'at and al-Sanusi's deep learning.

Imam al-Sanusi's mastery of the seven Quranic readings is validated through a documented chain of teachers and ijazas, typical of classical Islamic scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Sanusi invested enormous effort memorizing the seven qira'at through multiple complete recitations to his teachers. When you recite the Quran, do you feel a similar urgency to ensure your recitation is precisely as the Prophet ﷺ recited? What chain connects you to him, and are you satisfied with its quality?
?
The detailed documentation of teachers and licenses shows that knowledge of the Quran was not taken lightly. Is your relationship with the Quran one of casual recitation, or do you actively seek to know its authentic transmission? What would it take for you to find a teacher and receive an ijaza like al-Sanusi did?
?
If the chain of transmission for the Quran were broken today, the Book would be lost. Your own recitation is a link in that chain. How carefully do you maintain that link? Are you passing it on to others with the same precision? If not, what is holding you back?

Sanusi's Studies and Teachers in Various Sciences
Biography of Sanusi's teachers and sciences studied

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of Imam al-Sanusi's education across both transmitted and rational sciences, and his chain of teachers.

Core Idea
Sanusi's education bridged transmitted and rational sciences, establishing his authority.

This passage from the biography of Imam al-Sanusi details his studies under numerous scholars in various Islamic sciences, from Quranic recitation to logic and astronomy. It shows the comprehensive training that shaped his theological methodology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the detailed chain of teachers and the variety of sciences mentioned.
The passage begins with a quote from al-Balawi about qira'at (Quranic recitations).
2
Identify the sciences
List the different sciences Sanusi studied: qira'at, fiqh, usul, logic, bayan, hadith, tawhid, astronomy (astrolabe), inheritance, and arithmetic.
This shows his comprehensive education.
3
Trace the teachers
For each science, note the teacher's name and the nature of the study (reading, narration, license).
For example, he studied qira'at with Abu al-Hajjaj al-Sharif al-Hasani.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this diverse training might have influenced Sanusi's approach to theology, combining textual and rational disciplines.
This connects to his later works in kalam and tasawwuf.

وكان للإمام السنوسي علوٌّ كعب في جمع القراءات ؛ فقد قال العلامة أبو جعفر البلوي : ( أخذ القراءات السبع : عن الفقيه الأستاذ العالم العامل المحقق المقرئ أبي الحجاج يوسف بن الشيخ الصالح أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني تلاوةً عليه في ختمتين ، قال : وزدت من الثالثة قدراً صالحاً لم أتحقق الآن منتهاه جمعاً للسبعة بمضمن « التيسير » و « الشاطبية » وأجازه في المقارئ السبعة وفي غيرها من مروياته إجازة مطلقة عامة ، وحدثه بالسبع عن الإمامين العالمين المدرسين : الأستاذ الجليل الأعرف الأشهر المقرئ المحقق الأدرك الخاشع أبي العباس أحمد بن أبي عمران موسى اليزناسني ، والأستاذ الجليل المعظم الشهير المحقق الضابط المتقن النحوي اللغوي الحافظ الصالح الأزكى أبي العباس أحمد بن الفقيه العالم المتفنن أبي عبد الله محمد بن عيسى اللَّجائي ، قراءةً على الأول جمعاً في ختمة للسبعة ، قال : وزدت ثلاثة أحزاب من سورة البقرة ) ، وعلى الثاني لـ « فاتحة الكتاب » و « البقرة » وأوائل « آل عمران » جمعاً للسبع ، وإجازة فيما قرأ وفيما بقي ، حدثاه معاً بذلك عن الأستاذين : أبي عبد الله القيسي وأبي الحجاج بن مبخوت بسندهما ). ومن جملة العلماء الذين قرأ عليهم : الشيخ العلامة نصر الزواوي ، والشيخ العالم محمد بن تومرت الصنهاجي ، والشيخ الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني ، أخذ عنه القراءات السبع ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب ، أخذ عنه الفقه ، والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك ، أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب ، والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني ، قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه ، والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه ، قرأ عليه ( الرسالة ) ، وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي ( الإرشاد ) لإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد. واشتغل بالرواية وعلوم الأثر : على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي زيد عبد الرحمن الثعالبي ، فروى عنه ( الصحيحين ) وغيرهما من كتب الحديث والأثر ، وأجازه بما يجوز وعنه ، وأسمعه المسلسلات وغيرها. وقرأ الفرائض والحساب : على العلامة الجليل أبي الحسن القلصادي الأندلسي ، وأجازه بجميع ما يروي ، كما أجازه أيضاً ابن مرزوق الكفيف عن والده ابن مرزوق الحفيد.
And Imam al-Sanusi had high standing in the collection of the (seven) recitations; indeed, the scholar Abu Ja'far al-Balawi said: 'He took the seven recitations from the jurist, the professor, the scholar, the worker, the verifier, the reciter Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn al-Shaykh al-Salih Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani, reciting to him in two complete recitations. He said: I added from the third a fair amount whose extent I have not now verified, as a collection of the seven according to the content of al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. And he granted him a general absolute license in the seven recitations and in other things he narrated. And he narrated to him the seven from the two imams, the two scholars, the two teachers: the great, most famous, well-known, verifier, most perceptive, humble professor Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Abu 'Imran Musa al-Yaznasani, and the great, magnified, famous, verifier, precise, accurate, grammarian, linguist, memorizer, righteous, purest professor Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn the jurist, the scholar, the versatile Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn 'Isa al-Laja'i, reading to the first as a collection in one complete recitation for the seven, he said: I added three parts from Surat al-Baqara, and to the second for Surat al-Fatiha, al-Baqara, and the beginnings of Al 'Imran as a collection for the seven, and a license for what he read and for what remained. Both narrated to him together from the two professors: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Qaysi and Abu al-Hajjaj ibn Mabhut with their chains.' And among the scholars from whom he read: Shaykh al-'Allama Nasr al-Zawawi, and Shaykh al-'Alim Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji, and Shaykh al-Sharif Abu al-Hajjaj Yusuf ibn Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Sharif al-Hasani — he took from him the seven recitations; and Shaykh Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Isa al-Maghili famous as al-Jallab — he took from him jurisprudence; and the scholar, the justifier Abu 'Abd Allah al-Habbak — he took from him the science of the astrolabe; and Imam Muhammad ibn al-'Abbas al-Tilimsani — he read to him principles (usul), logic (mantiq), eloquence (bayan), and jurisprudence (fiqh); and the memorizer Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Taluti al-Ansari, his maternal brother — he read to him al-Risala; and he and this brother read to the pious, righteous imam Abu al-Qasim al-Kinabishi al-Irshad of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni and the science of divine unity. And he occupied himself with transmission and the sciences of tradition with the pious, righteous imam Abu Zayd 'Abd al-Rahman al-Tha'alabi, so he narrated from him the two Sahihs and other books of hadith and tradition, and he granted him a license for what is permissible and from him, and he made him hear the musalsalat and others. And he read inheritance laws and arithmetic with the great scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi al-Andalusi, and he granted him a license for all that he narrated, as also Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif granted him a license from his father Ibn Marzuq al-Hafid.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Imam al-Sanusi's extensive education under multiple scholars. It begins with a quote from al-Balawi detailing his studies in the seven Qur'anic recitations (qira'at) under Abu al-Hajjaj al-Sharif al-Hasani, who also narrated from two other teachers. Sanusi collected the recitations from al-Taysir and al-Shatibiyya. The passage then lists other scholars from whom Sanusi studied: Nasr al-Zawawi, Muhammad ibn Tumart al-Sanhaji, and again al-Sharif al-Hasani for qira'at; al-Maghili for fiqh; al-Habbak for astronomy; al-Tilimsani for usul, logic, bayan, and fiqh; al-Taluti for al-Risala; and al-Kinabishi for al-Irshad and 'ilm al-tawhid. Sanusi then studied hadith and transmission with al-Tha'alabi, narrating from him the two Sahihs and receiving licenses. Finally, he studied fara'id (inheritance) and hisab (arithmetic) with al-Qalasadi, and received a license from Ibn Marzuq al-Kafif through his father. This biography demonstrates Sanusi's comprehensive mastery of both transmitted (qira'at, hadith) and rational (logic, astronomy, usul) sciences, establishing his authority as a scholar.

Misconception: Sanusi was only a theologian specialized in kalam.
Correction: He studied a wide range of sciences including astronomy, logic, inheritance law, and Quranic recitations, as shown in this passage.

?
Your knowledge of Islam: is it as broad as Imam al-Sanusi's, covering both transmitted and rational sciences? Which subject have you neglected because it felt 'too hard' or 'unnecessary'? Will you commit to studying it this month?
?
Imam al-Sanusi sought out multiple teachers for different sciences. Who are the scholars you learn from? Are you content with just one source, or do you actively seek diverse teachers to avoid narrowness? Write down one new teacher or book you will turn to before this week ends.
?
You now see that Sanusi studied the astrolabe alongside theology. Are you afraid that studying secular sciences like astronomy or logic might weaken your faith? Or do you trust that truth is one? Identify one 'astrolabe' in your life—a worldly science you've avoided—and resolve to learn its basics for the sake of understanding Allah's signs.

Life of Imam al-Sanusi
beginner

The Comprehensive Education of Imam al-Sanusi
Lists Imam al-Sanusi's teachers and the subjects he studied.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of Imam al-Sanusi's traditional Islamic education, including his teachers and the diverse subjects he studied.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi mastered both transmitted and rational sciences from multiple renowned scholars.

Imam al-Sanusi is renowned as a theologian, but his education covered far more than theology. This passage from his biography lists his teachers in a range of disciplines, from Quranic recitation to arithmetic, showing the comprehensive nature of his learning. As you read, notice how he sought knowledge from different masters, each specializing in specific fields, and how he obtained formal authorization (ijaza) to transmit those sciences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the translation. Notice the pattern: each teacher is introduced with the subject studied.
The passage is a biographical list, so take note of each teacher-subject pair.
2
Identify the main teachers and subjects
List each teacher mentioned and the subject(s) al-Sanusi studied with them. Observe the diversity: Quran, fiqh, astronomy, logic, hadith, inheritance, etc.
There are many teachers, some with multiple subjects.
3
Understand the concept of ijaza
Notice that several teachers granted ijaza (permission to transmit). This was a formal certification in traditional learning.
Ijaza is not just a certificate but a chain of authorization back to the author.
4
Reflect on the educational journey
Consider how this broad foundation prepared al-Sanusi for his later theological works. Why might a theologian need to study astronomy or inheritance law?
This connects to the lesson's objective.

الشريف أبو الحجاج يوسف بن أبي العباس أحمد بن محمد الشريف الحسني ، أخذ عنه القراءات السبع ، والشيخ أبو عبد الله محمد بن أحمد بن عيسى المغيلي الشهير بالجلاب ، أخذ عنه الفقه ، والعالم المعدل أبو عبد الله الحباك ، أخذ عنه علم الأسطرلاب ، والإمام محمد بن العباس التلمساني ، قرأ عليه الأصول والمنطق والبيان والفقه ، والحافظ أبو الحسن علي بن محمد التالوتي الأنصاري أخوه لأمه ، قرأ عليه ( الرسالة » ، وقرأ هو وأخوه هذا على الإمام الورع الصالح أبي القاسم الكنابشي ( الإرشاد » لإمام الحرمين الجويني وعلم التوحيد

وقرأ الفرائض والحساب : على العلامة الجليل أبي الحسن القلصادي الأندلسي ، وأجازه بجميع ما يروي ، كما أجازه أيضاً ابن
مرزوق الكفيف عن والده ابن مرزوق الحفيد
قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم ومن أكابرهم : وليُّ الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصــالــح أبو علي الأحسـن المعـروف بـ «أبـركـان » ، والإمام أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن شيخنا أبي عبد الله بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به ) .
The noble Abū al-Ḥajjāj Yūsuf ibn Abī al-‘Abbās Aḥmad ibn Muḥammad al-Sharīf al-Ḥasanī – he (al-Sanūsī) took from him the seven readings (al-qirā’āt al-sab‘); and the shaykh Abū ‘Abd Allāh Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad ibn ‘Īsā al-Maghīlī known as al-Jallāb – he took from him jurisprudence (al-fiqh); and the upright scholar Abū ‘Abd Allāh al-Ḥabbāk – he took from him the science of the astrolabe (‘ilm al-asṭurlāb); and the imām Muḥammad ibn al-‘Abbās al-Tilimsānī – he read upon him uṣūl (principles), logic (al-manṭiq), rhetoric (al-bayān) and fiqh; and the ḥāfiẓ Abū al-Ḥasan ‘Alī ibn Muḥammad al-Tālūtī al-Anṣārī, his maternal brother – he read upon him ‘al-Risāla’ (the Epistle), and he and this brother of his read upon the pious, righteous imām Abū al-Qāsim al-Kinābishī ‘al-Irshād’ of Imām al-Ḥaramayn al-Juwaynī and the science of divine unity (‘ilm al-tawḥīd).
And he occupied himself with transmission (al-riwāya) and the sciences of hadith (‘ulūm al-athar) upon the pious, righteous imām Abū Zayd ‘Abd al-Raḥmān al-Tha‘ālibī – so he narrated from him the two Ṣaḥīḥs and other books of hadith and athar, and he (al-Tha‘ālibī) granted him permission (ijāza) for what he was permitted to transmit and from him, and he had him listen to the ‘musalsalāt’ (chains of transmission).
And he read farā’iḍ (inheritance laws) and ḥisāb (arithmetic) upon the great scholar Abū al-Ḥasan al-Qalṣādī al-Andalusī, and he granted him permission (ijāza) for all that he narrated, just as he was also granted permission by Ibn Marzūq al-Kafīf from his father Ibn Marzūq al-Ḥafīd.
The scholar al-Balawī said: “He took from the shaykhs of his town from a group of our shaykhs and others, and among their great ones: the saint of Allāh, the imām, the scholar, the righteous, Abū ‘Alī al-Aḥsan known as ‘Abarkān’; and the imām Abū ‘Abd Allāh ibn al-‘Abbās – though he did not take much from him and others; and he also took from our shaykh Abū ‘Abd Allāh ibn Marzūq, and our shaykh Abū al-Ḥasan al-Qalṣādī, and the jurist (faqīh) al-furū‘ī Abū ‘Abd Allāh al-Jullāb, and the majestic jurist Abū al-Faraj al-Ghurabilī, author of the verse abridgment of al-Mukhtaṣar – I think he took from him; and he took the science of arithmetic and inheritance from the eminent jurist in them, Abū ‘Abd Allāh ibn Tūmart; and he also took from his brother mentioned earlier, and from those whom his student, our companion, the eminent, accomplished, blessed jurist Abū ‘Abd Allāh Muḥammad ibn ‘Umar al-Mallālī included in the book introducing him.”
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a biographical enumeration listing Imam al-Sanūsī’s teachers and the subjects he studied. It begins by naming al-Sharīf Abū al-Ḥajjāj, from whom he learned the seven canonical Qur’anic readings. Next is Abū ‘Abd Allāh al-Maghīlī (al-Jallāb) for fiqh, then Abū ‘Abd Allāh al-Ḥabbāk for the science of the astrolabe. Then Imām Muḥammad al-Tilimsānī, with whom he studied uṣūl (principles of jurisprudence), logic, rhetoric, and fiqh. After that, his maternal brother al-Ḥāfiẓ Abū al-Ḥasan al-Tālūtī taught him the Risāla of Ibn Abī Zayd al-Qayrawānī. Together with his brother, he also read al-Irshād of al-Juwaynī and ‘ilm al-tawḥīd under Abū al-Qāsim al-Kinābishī. The passage then moves to his work in hadith: under Abū Zayd al-Tha‘ālibī, he narrated the two Ṣaḥīḥs and other books, received ijāza (authorization to transmit), and was made to hear the musalsalāt traditions. Next, he studied farā’iḍ (inheritance) and ḥisāb (arithmetic) under al-Qalṣādī, who granted him ijāza, as did Ibn Marzūq al-Kafīf from his father. Finally, a quote from al-Balawī adds further teachers: Abū ‘Alī al-Aḥsan (called Abarkān), Abū ‘Abd Allāh ibn al-‘Abbās, Ibn Marzūq, al-Qalṣādī again, al-Jullāb, al-Ghurābilī, Ibn Tūmart, and his own brother. The passage concludes by noting that al-Sanūsī’s student al-Mallālī compiled these teachers in a book about him. This passage demonstrates the vast scope of al-Sanūsī’s education, covering Qur’an, fiqh, astronomy, logic, rhetoric, uṣūl, hadith, inheritance, and arithmetic, and shows that he sought knowledge from multiple renowned scholars of his time, receiving both direct study and licenses to transmit.

Imam al-Sanusi's Spiritual Training and Ethical Upbringing
Describes the primary spiritual influence on Imam al-Sanusi, Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the central role of Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi in shaping Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual training and that his education encompassed both exoteric sciences and esoteric discipline.

Core Idea
Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual upbringing under Shaykh al-Tazi combined scholarly excellence with saintly manners.

This passage from the biography of Imam al-Sanusi highlights the person who most influenced his spiritual development. While many great scholars shaped his mind, it was Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi who left the deepest mark on his soul. Through this passage, we see that al-Sanusi's training was not merely academic but also included the inner sciences of tasawwuf.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Pay attention to the heading 'Sufism and his ethical upbringing.'
2
Identify the key figure
Notice that the passage singles out Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi as the greatest spiritual influence. He is described as a saint (wali), gnostic (arif), and righteous (salih).
3
Understand the dual nature of his influence
Observe that al-Tazi excelled both in exoteric sciences (Qur'an, language, hadith, fiqh) and in the manners of the saints. This shows that spiritual training complements scholarly learning.
4
Reflect on the quote
The quote from al-Tanbakti emphasizes the transmission of dhikr (remembrance) and the use of prayer beads through the spiritual chain from al-Tazi. This indicates a formal Sufi lineage.
The phrase 'it suffices for you' suggests the value of this transmission.
5
Connect to the broader context
Understand that Imam al-Sanusi's education was holistic, integrating outward knowledge with inward purification. This balanced approach is a hallmark of Sunni orthodoxy.
This lesson corrects the misconception that his training was purely academic.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تصوف و تربيته الأخلاقية
هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي يظهر أنَّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي نزيل وهران.. كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من هذا الجانب ؛ فإلى إمامته في علوم القرآن وعلم اللسان ، وحفظ الأحاديث ، وسعة علمه بالفقه وأصوله ، وحِدَّة نظره وفهمه .. كان ممتعاً بآداب الأولياء والكُمَّل ، نقل العلامة التنبكتي في «نيل الابتهاج » عن ابن صعد صاحب ( النجم الثاقب » : ( وحسبك من
السبحة وتلقين الذكر من طريق شيخه أبي إسحاق إبراهيم التازي )
Sufism and his ethical upbringing. There are great gnostic personalities by whom Imam al-Sanūsī was influenced, but what appears is that the shaykh, the saint, the gnostic, the righteous Ibrāhīm ibn Muḥammad ibn ‘Alī al-Tāzī, resident of Wahran, was the one with the greatest impact on Imam al-Sanūsī from this aspect; for in addition to his imamate in the sciences of the Qur’an and the science of language, his memorization of hadiths, the breadth of his knowledge of jurisprudence and its principles, and the sharpness of his insight and understanding… he was endowed with the manners of the saints (awliyā’) and the perfect ones (kummal). The scholar al-Tanbakti transmitted in his work ‘Nayl al-Ibtihāj’ from Ibn Ṣa‘d, author of ‘al-Najm al-Thāqib’: “And it suffices for you from the prayer beads (al-subaḥa) and the imparting of the dhikr through the path of his shaykh Abū Isḥāq Ibrāhīm al-Tāzī.”
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage discusses the spiritual and ethical training of Imam al-Sanūsī. It begins with a heading: 'Sufism and his ethical upbringing.' The text then notes that many great gnostic personalities influenced him, but the one who had the greatest impact in this regard was Shaykh Ibrāhīm al-Tāzī, a saint (walī), gnostic (‘ārif), and righteous man who resided in Wahran (Oran). Al-Tāzī was not only an imam in Qur’anic sciences, linguistics, hadith memorization, fiqh and its principles, and possessed sharp insight; he was also adorned with the manners of the awliyā’ and the kummal (the elect who have perfected themselves). The passage then quotes al-Tanbakti’s Nayl al-Ibtihāj, citing Ibn Ṣa‘d from al-Najm al-Thāqib: 'And it suffices for you from the prayer beads (al-subaḥa) and the imparting (talqīn) of the dhikr through the chain of his shaykh Abū Isḥāq Ibrāhīm al-Tāzī.' This indicates that al-Sanūsī received the transmission of the Sufi practice of dhikr and the use of prayer beads from this spiritual lineage, showing that his education was not limited to exoteric sciences but also included esoteric training.

Imam al-Sanusi's spiritual training under Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi integrated exoteric scholarship with esoteric discipline, forming a holistic Islamic education.

What concrete steps can you take to find such a guide, or to cultivate those qualities in yourself if you are a teacher?
?

?

Sanusi's Teachers and His Education
Al-Balawi enumerates Sanusi's teachers in various disciplines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key teachers from whom Imam Sanusi studied and the subjects he learned from each.

Core Idea
Imam Sanusi's education was shaped by a diverse group of scholars across multiple disciplines.

This passage from al-Balawi provides a biographical glimpse into Imam Sanusi's scholarly formation. It lists several teachers and the subjects he studied with them, showing the breadth of his education. As you read, notice the variety of disciplines mentioned—from fiqh to arithmetic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the overall meaning.
The passage is a list of names; pay attention to the descriptions of each teacher.
2
Identify each teacher and their specialty
Go through each name and note what the text says about them. Some are described as jurists, others as teachers of arithmetic.
Not all teachers have a specialty mentioned; some are just named.
3
Notice the subject of arithmetic and inheritance law
The text explicitly states that Sanusi learned arithmetic and inheritance law from Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart. This shows the scope of his studies.
These are rational sciences (ma'qulat) alongside transmitted sciences.
4
Reflect on the significance of studying under multiple teachers
Consider why Sanusi studied under so many different teachers. This was the traditional method of seeking knowledge from specialists.
It also reflects the richness of the scholarly environment in Tlemcen.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال العلامة البلوي : ( وأخذ من شيوخ بلده عن جماعة من أشياخنا وغيرهم ومن أكابرهم : وليُّ الله سبحانه الإمام العالم الصــالــح أبو علي الأحسـن المعـروف بـ «أبـركـان » ، والإمام أبو عبد الله بن العباس ولم يكثر عنه وغيرهم ، وأخذ أيضاً عن شيخنا أبي عبد الله بن مرزوق ، وشيخنا أبي الحسن القلصادي ، والفقيه الفروعي أبي عبد الله الجلاب ، والفقيه الجليل أبي الفرج الغرابلي صاحب نظم المختصر » ، أظنه أخذ عنه ، وأخذ علم الحساب والفرائض عن الفقيه المبرز فيهما أبي عبد الله بن تومرت ، وأخذ أيضاً عن أخيه المتقدم ذكره ، وعن هؤلاء ممن ضمنه تلميذه صاحبنا الفقيه الأجل المحصل المبارك أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر الملالي في كتاب التعريف به ) .
Al-Allama al-Balawi said: He (Sanusi) took from the scholars of his town from a group of our teachers and others, and among their most prominent: the saint of Allah, the Imam, the learned, the righteous Abu Ali al-Ahsan, known as 'Abarkan', and Imam Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas, but he did not take much from him, and others. He also took from our teacher Abu Abdullah ibn Marzuq, and our teacher Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, and the jurist in branches of fiqh Abu Abdullah al-Jallab, and the noble jurist Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili, author of the poetic abridgment (Nazm al-Mukhtasar); I think he took from him. And he took the science of arithmetic and inheritance law from the jurist eminent in both, Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart. He also took from his brother mentioned previously, and from those whom his student, our companion the noble, accomplished, and blessed jurist Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar al-Mallali, included in the book 'al-Ta'rif bihi'.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biographical enumeration of Imam Sanusi's teachers, cited from al-Allama al-Balawi. It lists several scholars from whom Sanusi studied, covering various Islamic sciences. The list includes: (1) Abu Ali al-Ahsan known as Abarkan, (2) Abu Abdullah ibn al-Abbas (though limited), (3) Abu Abdullah ibn Marzuq, (4) Abu al-Hasan al-Qalasadi, (5) Abu Abdullah al-Jallab (a jurist specializing in furu'), (6) Abu al-Faraj al-Gharabili (who authored a poetic abridgment of a fiqh text), (7) Abu Abdullah ibn Tumart (teacher of arithmetic and inheritance law), and his brother. The passage concludes by noting that Sanusi's student Muhammad al-Mallali compiled these teachers in his work 'al-Ta'rif bihi'.

The Virtues of Ibrahim al-Tazi and His Influence on Sanusi
Praises Ibrahim al-Tazi's virtues and his impact on Sanusi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the exemplary character of Ibrahim al-Tazi and why he was such a profound influence on Imam Sanusi's spiritual development.

Core Idea
Ibrahim al-Tazi's character was so noble that his name became a proverb for wisdom and patience.

Imam Sanusi was shaped by many spiritual masters, but none left a deeper imprint than Ibrahim al-Tazi. This passage highlights al-Tazi's extraordinary virtues—his knowledge, forbearance, and saintly conduct—showing why contemporaries compared others to him. The text sets the stage for understanding the spiritual lineage that Sanusi inherited.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage aloud
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its rhythm. Then read the translation to ensure comprehension.
Notice the flowing praise and the use of proverbs.
2
Identify al-Tazi's attributes
List the qualities attributed to al-Tazi: mastery of Qur'anic sciences, linguistics, hadith, fiqh, usul, sharp intellect, saintly character.
3
Understand the proverbs
The text mentions two proverbs: one praising his intellect and forbearance, another showing how people wished they had his patience. Reflect on what these reveal about his societal impact.
These proverbs indicate his legendary status.
4
Connect to Sanusi
Consider why such a figure would be the most influential on Sanusi. The passage says he had the 'greatest impact' on Sanusi's moral training.
This lesson focuses on al-Tazi's character; the next lesson covers the transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تصوف و تربيته الأخلاقية
هناك شخصيات عرفانية كبيرة تأثر بها الإمام السنوسي ، لكن الذي يظهر أنَّ الشيخ الولي العارف الصالح إبراهيم بن محمد بن علي التازي نزيل وهران.. كان صاحب الأثر الأكبر في الإمام السنوسي من هذا الجانب ؛ فإلى إمامته في علوم القرآن وعلم اللسان ، وحفظ الأحاديث ، وسعة علمه بالفقه وأصوله ، وحِدَّة نظره وفهمه .. كان ممتعاً بآداب الأولياء والكُمَّل ، نقل العلامة التنبكتي في «نيل الابتهاج » عن ابن صعد صاحب ( النجم الثاقب » : ( وحسبك من جلالته وسعادته : أنَّ المثل ضرب بعقله وحلمه ، واشتهر في الآفاق ذكر فضله وعلمه حتى الآن ؛ إذا بالغ أحد في وصف رجل قال : كأنه سيدي إبراهيم التازي ، وإذا امتلأ أحدهم غيظاً قال : لو كنتُ في منزلة سيدي إبراهيم التازي ما صبرتُ لهذا ؛ لما كان يتحمله من إذاية الخلق ، والصبر على المكاره ، واصطناع المعروف للناس والمداراة ، فهو أحد من أظهره الله لهداية خلقه ، وأقامه داعياً لبسط كراماته ، مجللاً برداء المحبة والمهابة ، مع ما له من القبول في قلوب الخاصة والعامة ؛ فدعاهم إلى الله ببصيرة ، وأرشدهم لعبوديته بعقائد التوحيد ووظائف الأذكار ((۱) وكان من نعيم الإمام السنوسي : صحبته لهذا العارف الجليل ، وانتسابه له ، وقد شاركه في هذا أعلام ؛ كأخيه لأمه الشيخ علي التالوتي ، والحافظ التنسي ، والإمام أحمد زروق قال العلامة المؤرخ ابن مريم المليتي في ( البستان في ذكر الأولياء والعلماء بتلمسان » : ( أخذ عن الإمام العلامة الولي الزاهد الناصح إبراهيم التازي نزيل وهران ؛ ألبسه الخرقة ، وحدثه بها عن شيوخه ، وبصق في فيه ، وروى عنه أشياء كثيرة ((٢) والعارف التازي قد لبس الخرقة على طريقة السادة الصوفية من
Sufism and his moral training. There are great gnostic personalities by whom Imam Sanusi was influenced, but it appears that the righteous saintly gnostic Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tazi, resident of Oran, had the greatest impact on Imam Sanusi in this aspect. For besides his imamate in the Qur'anic sciences, linguistics, memorization of hadith, vast knowledge of fiqh and its principles, and sharpness of insight and understanding, he was endowed with the etiquettes of the saints and the perfect ones. Al-Allama al-Tanbakti transmitted in 'Nayl al-Ibtihaj' from Ibn Sa'd, author of 'al-Najm al-Thaqib': 'Sufficient for you regarding his majesty and felicity is that proverbs were made about his intellect and forbearance, and mention of his virtue and knowledge spread across the horizons until now. If someone exaggerated in describing a man, he would say: He is like my master Ibrahim al-Tazi. And if one of them became filled with rage, he would say: If I were in the position of my master Ibrahim al-Tazi, I would not have tolerated this.' Because of what he endured from the harm of people, patience in hardships, doing good to people and showing forbearance. So he is one whom Allah manifested for the guidance of His creation, and established him as a caller to spread his miracles, wrapped in the garment of love and awe, with acceptance in the hearts of elite and commoners. So he called them to Allah with insight, and guided them to His servitude through the doctrines of tawhid and the functions of dhikr. And among the blessings of Imam Sanusi was his companionship with this noble gnostic, and his affiliation to him. And some prominent figures shared this with him, like his maternal brother Shaykh Ali al-Taluti, al-Hafiz al-Tansi, and Imam Ahmad Zarruq. The historian al-Allama Ibn Maryam al-Maliti said in 'al-Bustan fi Dhikr al-Awliya' wa al-Ulama' bi Tilimsan': 'He (Sanusi) took from the Imam, the scholar, the saint, the ascetic, the advisor Ibrahim al-Tazi, resident of Oran. He (al-Tazi) clothed him with the cloak (khirqa), and narrated it to him from his teachers, and blew into his mouth, and transmitted many things from him.' And the gnostic al-Tazi wore the cloak according to the way of the Sufi masters from.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage discusses the spiritual and moral training of Imam Sanusi, focusing on the influence of the Sufi master Ibrahim al-Tazi. It first states that although Sanusi was influenced by many great gnostic figures, al-Tazi had the greatest impact. The passage then describes al-Tazi's virtues: his mastery of Qur'anic sciences, linguistics, hadith, fiqh and usul, and his sharp intellect. Moreover, he possessed the noble character of the saints. A quotation from al-Tanbakti illustrates the high regard people had for al-Tazi, using proverbs to praise his intellect and forbearance. Al-Tazi's patience and goodness are highlighted. The passage then notes Sanusi's privilege of companionship with al-Tazi, and lists other notable figures who were also his companions. Finally, a quotation from Ibn Maryam provides a specific account: al-Tazi gave Sanusi the Sufi cloak (khirqa), transmitted it from his own teachers, blew into his mouth (a blessing), and transmitted many things. The text ends mentioning that al-Tazi himself wore the cloak according to the Sufi path.

Key Terms
إبراهيم التازي
نيل الابتهاج
العلامة التنبكتي
ابن صعد
التواضع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Tazi's influence was minor or merely scholarly.
Correction: The passage explicitly states he had the greatest impact on Sanusi's moral training, and his virtues were legendary even among contemporaries.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the proverbs regarding Ibrahim al-Tazi?
A) They were about his wealth
B) They were about his intellect and forbearance
C) They were about his physical strength
D) They were about his lineage

Key Takeaway
Ibrahim al-Tazi's character was so exemplary that people used his name as a standard for wisdom and patience, and he became the primary spiritual influence on Imam Sanusi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibrahim al-Tazi was known for his immense patience despite being harmed by people. Think of a situation where you were recently wronged. Did you react with immediate anger or did you practice forbearance? What specific step can you take today to bear harm with patience like al-Tazi?
?
People made proverbs about al-Tazi's intellect and forbearance. If your life were distilled into a proverb, what virtue would it express? Is that the virtue you want to be known for, and if not, what will you do today to change that?
?
Al-Tazi was 'wrapped in the garment of love and awe' of Allah, which made him beloved to elite and commoners. Do you—honestly—wake up with love and awe of Allah that directs your daily choices? What one action can you commit to this week to strengthen that garment in your life?

Sanusi's Affiliation and the Transmission of the Sufi Cloak
Details Sanusi's companionship with al-Tazi and the transmission of the khirqa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi formally affiliated with Ibrahim al-Tazi through the transmission of the Sufi cloak (khirqa) and what this signified.

Core Idea
Sanusi received the Sufi cloak from al-Tazi, symbolizing spiritual lineage and blessing.

After describing al-Tazi's virtues, the passage turns to Sanusi's personal connection. It lists other companions of al-Tazi and then presents a historical account: al-Tazi clothed Sanusi with the khirqa, blew into his mouth, and transmitted knowledge. This ritual cemented Sanusi's place in the spiritual chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the names of other disciples mentioned.
2
Identify the transmission elements
Identify three actions by al-Tazi: clothing with khirqa, blowing into mouth, transmitting traditions.
The khirqa is a symbol of spiritual authority.
3
Understand the significance
Reflect on the meaning of 'blowing into the mouth' as a blessing and transmission of spiritual state.
It is not a medical act but a traditional blessing.
4
Connect to Sanusi's lineage
This act formally linked Sanusi to the spiritual chain (silsila) of al-Tazi and his teachers.

What did Ibrahim al-Tazi give to Sanusi according to Ibn Maryam?

B) A Sufi cloak (khirqa)
C) A rosary (subha)
D) A book of dhikr

Key Takeaway
Sanusi received the Sufi cloak from al-Tazi, which symbolized spiritual lineage and transmission of blessings, formally linking him to the Sufi chain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In my pursuit of knowledge and spiritual growth, do I sincerely seek out and attach myself to qualified teachers who can transmit both knowledge and blessing, or do I rely on self-study and sporadic inspiration?
?
This lesson shows that Sanusi received a physical cloak as part of a spiritual transmission. Have I ever reduced a sacred symbol or ritual to an empty form, missing the reality of the blessing and lineage it represents?
?
If I were offered the opportunity to receive a spiritual inheritance from a living saint, would I humble myself to receive it, or would pride or skepticism keep me at a distance? What would I have to change in my heart to truly accept such a gift?

The Virtues of Ibrahim al-Tazi and His Connection to al-Sanusi
Biographical account of Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi and al-Sanusi's connection to him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spiritual and educational role of Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi in Imam al-Sanusi's life and the significance of the khirqa transmission.

Core Idea
A saint's example is a living proof of divine guidance.

This passage introduces us to a key spiritual figure in al-Sanusi's life: Shaykh Ibrahim al-Tazi. Through a vivid description of his character and the blessings he received, we learn how the chain of spiritual transmission worked in the Maghrib. This is not abstract theology but living tradition, establishing the author's own lineage and authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without interpreting. Then read the translation. Notice the hyperbolic descriptions of al-Tazi's character.
The text uses proverbial language: 'like my master Ibrahim al-Tazi'.
2
Identify the virtues of al-Tazi
List the qualities attributed to al-Tazi: intellect, forbearance, patience, doing good, diplomacy. See how these made him a model for others.
These are not just personal traits; they are signs of his sainthood (wilaya).
3
Trace the chain of the khirqa
Identify the sequence of transmission: al-Sanusi from al-Tazi, al-Tazi from Sharaf al-Din al-Da'i, al-Da'i from Salih al-Zawawi, and back to Abu Madyan.
The khirqa symbolizes spiritual authorization and blessing.
4
Reflect on al-Sanusi's place
Notice that al-Sanusi's companionship with al-Tazi is called 'one of his blessings'. This shows the importance of spiritual lineage in Islamic scholarship.
Other notable scholars also took from al-Tazi, showing he was a major figure.
